## Domain Knowledge (LLM-generated)
**Domain**: nonlinear dynamics / nonlinear oscillators
**Analysis**: This task involves finding the equation of motion (acceleration) for a nonlinear harmonic oscillator. The acceleration dv_dt is determined by restoring forces (dependent on x), damping forces (dependent on v), and possibly periodic driving forces (dependent on t).

**Common formula structures in this domain**:
- Simple harmonic oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x (linear restoring force)
- Damped harmonic oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v (linear restoring + linear damping)
- Duffing oscillator (undriven): dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 (cubic nonlinear restoring force)
- Duffing oscillator with damping: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * v (cubic restoring + damping)
- Driven Duffing oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * v + c3 * cos(c4 * t) (with periodic driving)
- Van der Pol oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * (1 - c2 * x**2) * v (nonlinear damping)
- Quintic nonlinear oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * x**5 (higher-order restoring force)
- Softening/hardening spring with drive: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**2 + c2 * v + c3 * sin(c4 * t)
- Pendulum-like: dv_dt = c0 * sin(c1 * x) (nonlinear restoring from sine potential)
- Damped pendulum with drive: dv_dt = c0 * sin(c1 * x) + c2 * v + c3 * cos(c4 * t)
- Quadratic damping: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v * abs(v) (velocity-squared damping)
- Nonlinear damping + cubic spring: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * v + c3 * v**3
- Rayleigh oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v + c2 * v**3 (cubic velocity nonlinearity)
- Coupled position-velocity: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x * v + c2 * v (multiplicative coupling)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Odd-power restoring forces (x, x³, x⁵) preserve symmetry of oscillation about equilibrium — use when system has symmetric potential
- Even-power position terms (x²) break symmetry and indicate asymmetric potential wells or quadratic nonlinearity
- Velocity-dependent terms proportional to (1 - x²)*v indicate amplitude-dependent damping (self-sustained oscillations like Van der Pol)
- Sinusoidal functions of position sin(c*x) indicate a periodic potential (e.g., pendulum dynamics) rather than polynomial restoring force
- Explicit time dependence through sin(c*t) or cos(c*t) indicates externally driven/forced oscillation
- Products x*v suggest energy-dependent or phase-space coupling terms that can produce limit cycles
- Cubic velocity terms v³ paired with linear velocity terms indicate Rayleigh-type nonlinear dissipation
- Absence of explicit time dependence suggests an autonomous system where energy is conserved or dissipated monotonically
- Multiple frequency components in driving (e.g., cos(c1*t) + cos(c2*t)) suggest quasi-periodic or parametric forcing
